enforcement infrastructure in Firefox is structured across multiple specialized files in the dom/security/ directory:\\n\\n1. **CSP Directive Parser**: The nsCSPParser class (dom/security/nsCSPParser.h and nsCSPParser.cpp) is responsible for parsing CSP policies from string directives into a structured format. The parseContentSecurityPolicy() static method tokenizes and parses the policy string according to CSP grammar specifications.\\n\\n2. **Main CSP Context**: The nsCSPContext class (dom/security/nsCSPContext.h and nsCSPContext.cpp) implements the nsIContentSecurityPolicy XPCOM interface and serves as the primary container for CSP policies. It holds an array of nsCSPPolicy objects and is responsible for policy enforcement decisions through methods like ShouldLoad() for resource loads and GetAllowsInline() for inline script/style evaluation.\\n\\n3. **CSP Utilities and Directives**: The nsCSPUtils.h and nsCSPUtils.cpp files contain the core directive classes including nsCSPDirective (base class), nsCSPScriptSrcDirective (for script-src evaluation), and nsCSPStyleSrcDirective. The nsCSPScriptSrcDirective class specifically handles inline script allowance evaluation through its allows() and allowsAllInlineBehavior() methods. It also manages worker restrictions and script element/attribute restrictions.\\n\\n4. **XPCOM Interface Declaration**: The nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl file (located at dom/interfaces/security/) declares the XPCOM interface with CSPDirective enums and methods for querying CSP allowances. This interface is implemented by nsCSPContext.\\n\\n5. **Inline Script Evaluation**: Script-src evaluation for inline scripts is performed through the nsCSPScriptSrcDirective class which evaluates against nonce, hash, and keyword sources (unsafe-inline, strict-dynamic). The GetAllowsInline() method in nsCSPContext checks directives like SCRIPT_SRC_ELEM_DIRECTIVE and SCRIPT_SRC_ATTR_DIRECTIVE for inline allowance.\\n\\n6. **Eval Checking**: The CSPEvalChecker class (dom/security/CSPEvalChecker.h and CSPEvalChecker.cpp) provides static methods CheckForWindow() and CheckForWorker() to verify whether eval() operations are permitted by the CSP, checking against the script-src directive's restriction on unsafe-eval.\\n\\n7. **Violation Reporting**: CSP violations are reported through ReportInlineViolation() and ReportViolation() methods in nsCSPContext, with violation details stored in CSPViolationData structures (dom/security/CSPViolationData.h and CSPViolationData.cpp) that capture blocked content source type, effective directive, source location, and optional script hash samples.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
